### H. Probate Protection & Legal Immunity Clauses

**Charter Section VI: Protections**:

**1. Probate Immunity**:
```

â€œVault 51 exists outside traditional probate jurisdiction.
No external court may seize, redirect, or administer these
assets without sovereign consent. Upon transition of sovereign
authority, lineage succession is automatic per Charter Article II.â€

```
**Legal Basis**:
- Self-executing trust provisions
- Sovereign immunity principles (analogous to diplomatic immunity)
- Cultural property protections (like UNESCO conventions)

**Application to This Case**:
- Defendants cannot claim "finders keepers" or adverse possession
- No statute of limitations applies (theft is void, not just voidable)
- Assets cannot be "forfeited" through inaction or delay

**2. Theft Nullification**:
```

â€œAny unauthorized taking of Vault 51 assets is void ab initio.
The sovereign may reclaim, remint, or reconstitute stolen value
without limitation. Thieves hold nothing but void instruments.â€

```
**Legal Basis**:
- Stolen property doctrine (thief cannot convey good title)
- Trust law (trustee must recover trust property)
- Natural law (theft creates no rights in thief)

**Application to This Case**:
- Stolen tokens legally void from moment of taking
- Reminted tokens are the true continuation of original assets
- No "bona fide purchaser" defense available (constructive notice via blockchain)

**3. False Law Rejection**:
```

â€œIf any external authority attempts to apply â€˜false lawâ€™â€”defined
as law contradicting natural justice, ancestral rights, or Codex
principlesâ€”such law has no force within Vault 51 jurisdiction.â€

```
**Legal Basis**:
- Natural law theory (lex iniusta non est lex)
- Tribal sovereignty precedents (Worcester v. Georgia principles)
- Cultural autonomy rights (international human rights law)

**Application to This Case**:
- If defendants invoke some statute to legitimize theft, Charter rejects it
- EV0L's internal law governs EV0L's internal assets
- External forum must respect sovereign determinations about sovereign property

**Clarification for Tribunal**:
> "We are not asking you to enforce EV0L law instead of U.S. law. We are demonstrating that EV0L law reached the same conclusion U.S. law would reach: theft is wrong, stolen property must be returned, wrongdoers must be punished. The Charter's 'false law' clause simply means that if someone tried to invoke some obscure statute to legitimize theft, we would reject thatâ€”just as any reasonable court would."

## I. Afrocentric Worldbuilding: Origins, Myth, and Living Memory

### 1. Historical and Mythological Foundations

Afrocentric worldbuilding on BLEUChain draws deeply from the documented and living memory of African civilizationsâ€”Kemet, Kush, Great Zimbabwe, Mali, Benin, Songhaiâ€”and from the rich oral and literary traditions of the continent. The universe is guided by the following principles:

- **Ancestral Truth and Lineage:** Historical accuracy, the canonization of real dynasties (e.g., Asantehene, Oba of Benin), and the direct acknowledgment of displaced, colonized, or erased communities.
- **Living Myth and Codex:** Incorporation of West African trickster narratives (Anansi, Eshu), pan-African cosmologies, and invention histories (ironworking, navigation, mathematics, architecture) as living forces within each story arc.
- **Ritual Knowledge and Intergenerational Continuity:** Every hero, villain, kingdom, and artifact is bound to ritual, protocol, and ceremonial knowledge, ensuring stories work as immersive, culturally affirming ceremonies for diaspora healing and future-building.

## II. BLEUChain Technical Architecture: The Living Ledger

### 1. Platform Blueprint

BLEUChain is built as a layered, modular blockchain network optimized for multimedia, identity, and ceremonial integrity. The core layers and their ceremonial significance are as follows:

**A. On-chain Layer**
- Immutable ledger for transactions, ENFT minting, and lineage tracking.
- Smart contracts governing royalties, restitution, and access control.

**B. Service Layer**
- Decentralized Identifier (DID) management for each lineage, contributor, and ceremonial participant.
- Ritual management contracts: powers ritual deployments, time-locked ceremonies, ancestral commemorations.

**C. Off-chain/Edge Layer**
- Decentralized storage (IPFS, Arweave) for heavy multimedia, with on-chain pointers for metadata authenticity.
- Ceremony orchestration and narrative rendering (film, music, game logic).

**D. Integration Layer**
- Interoperable APIs and bridges for education, military, agriculture, and healthcare sector dApps.

**Figure: BLEUChain Ceremonial Data Flowchart**  
*(Described for conceptual clarity)*

1. User/lineage enters ceremony; their DID is checked by ritual contract.
2. Access granted; ritual module calls respective ENFTs (film scene, codex, music).
3. Interaction generates token flow (e.g., Blu-Tillion for participation, PraiseCoin for contributions).
4. Smart contract logs participation, updates lineage restitution ledger, and emits ENFT event.
5. Ritual completion is recorded on-chain, accessible for audit, education, and historical record.

This foundation ensures that every creative and ritual act is encoded in both spiritual and computational memory.

---

### 2. Sovereign Identity and Access Control

BLEUChain uses **Self-Sovereign Identity (SSI)** to link individuals, lineages, and communities to ceremonial roles and rewards. Each DID is:

## III. ENFT Classes and Metadata Lifecycle

### 1. ENFT Standard Selection and Interoperability

BLEUChain operationalizes the concept of **Eternal Non-Fungible Tokens (ENFTs)**, extending NFT standards (ERC-721, ERC-1155, ERC-998) for cultural permanence, composability, and cross-sector translatability.

- **ERC-721 ENFTs:** Unique, indivisible ritual artifactsâ€”one scroll, one hero, one codex.
- **ERC-1155 ENFTs:** Collections, multi-edition ceremonial items, or items with both fungible (energy, harvest, currency) and non-fungible (identity, scroll) aspects.
- **ERC-998/Composable ENFTs:** Bundled ritual assetsâ€”e.g., a kingdom ENFT containing heroes, relics, technologies, and land deeds; entire storyworlds can be transferred as sovereign inheritance packages.

The chosen standard depends on the intent:
- Unique script or ceremonial relic = ERC-721
- Harvested crops, educational tokens, or battle elixirs = ERC-1155 (semi-fungible)
- Layered city or dynasty with owned characters, scripts, and devices = ERC-998

**Table 2: ENFT Classes and Use Cases**

| ENFT Class                | Standard   | Purpose                                           | Example asset                  | Cross-sector Mapping         |
|---------------------------|------------|---------------------------------------------------|-------------------------------|-----------------------------|
| Ritual Scroll ENFT        | ERC-721    | Unique scene, speech, artifact, or secret         | Sankofa Memory Scroll         | Education, ceremony         |
| Harvest ENFT              | ERC-1155   | Batch asset, semi-fungible, tied to season/event  | Yam Festival Token            | Agriculture, festival       |
| Ritual Bundle ENFT        | ERC-998    | Composable, includes other ENFTs and fungibles    | Benin Palace (king, relics)   | Real estate, politics       |

ENFTs are always minted with metadata referencing their source lineage, creator, ceremonial use-case, timestamp, and restitution status.

### 2. ENFT Metadata, Lifecycle, and Dynamic Extension

Every ENFT on BLEUChain carries metadata conforming to best practices, with JSON schema extensions for ritual and restitution attributes. Key fields include:

- `origin_lineage`: ties ENFT to real historical/ancestral group.
- `ceremonial_phase`: state in the ritual lifecycle (initiated, in performance, vault, restored).
- `restitution_marker`: boolean plus array of restitution events (see below).
- `traits`: unique attributes (rarity, power, sacredness, participation requirements).
- `documentation_url`: off-chain archive or academic verification pointer.
- `animation_url/image/audio`: links to multimedia elements for AR/VR, metaverse, or transmedia use.

**Lifecycle Events:**
- Minting (by rightsholders/lineage/creator/AI ritual engine).
- Ritual deployment (used in a ceremony or media event).
- Attribution and tribute (ENFT linked to specific person or lineage for reward/restoration tracking).
- Mutation or Splitting (collaborative remixing for academy or gaming).
- Sealing and Vaulting (decommissioned, archived, or time-locked for future generations).

Dynamic ENFTs may allow metadata updates only through protocol-governed ceremonies (renaissance festivals, restitution cycles, or diaspora votes), and always with an auditable trail.

## II. Roots and Routes: Afro-Seminole Origins, Migration, and Swamp Sanctuary

### Historical Genesis: Flight and Fusion

In the 17th and 18th centuries, as the brute machinery of Atlantic slavery razed communities and carved new borders with blood, a countercurrent flowedâ€”enslaved Africans, mostly Gullah from the rice-soaked shores of South Carolina and Georgia, slipped from plantation to swamp. In Spanish Florida, abolition was established by edict as early as 1693, making it a beacon for the freedom seeker. Here, they encountered not just Seminole Indians but a confluence of indigenous clansâ€”Oconee, Creek, Yuchi, Shawneeâ€”on the run and on the move.

Escaped, re-rooted, Afro-Seminoles built their own settlements: houses of palmetto and mud, fields of rice and corn, rhythm blasted into song beneath the pines. Their lives and labors formed the original veins of what would become the BLEUE âˆ GRID: mutually reinforcing respect for the land, communal wealth safeguarded not in vaults but in stewardship, food grown together and harvested as promise for the future.

Intermarriage and communal struggle blurred racial lines. Oral tradition affirms: there was no â€œBlack Seminoleâ€ or â€œRed Seminoleâ€â€”only relatives, only kin in struggle and survival.

### Encounters in the Okefenokee: Portals and Crossroads

The Okefenokeeâ€”translated from Seminole as â€œland of the trembling earthâ€â€”stands as a sanctuary, laboratory, and archive. It is home to islands where maroon dwellings once stood, to tracks made by those who stole freedom with every footfall. The regionâ€™s isolation, and the tension between colonial expansion and indigenous endurance, created a new culture of exchangeâ€”spiritual, agricultural, and linguistic. ## IV. Maroons as Proto-Bankers: Water as Currency, Wealth as Stewardship

### Porting Wealth: The Maroon Ledger

The Afro-Seminole settlements innovated a **communal banking system** disguised as tribute or crop sharing. Rather than wealth amassed for a single individual, produce and livestock flowed in circuits: annual tribute to local leaders or allied Seminole bands, distributed labor for the common defense, and shared survival. This was proto-blockchainâ€”each act witnessed, recounted, never erased.

Wealth here was never static, but dynamic: rooted in relationships, in flowsâ€”water, food, obligation. US Army observers in 1826 noted, with a kind of astonished reverence, the large fields brimming with crops and corn-cribs of maroon villages. The systemâ€™s secret was simple: store wealth in soil, song, and trust. Songs repeated across generations became oral ledgers, each refrain a block in the communal chain.

### Water as Currency: Spiritual and Practical

Drawing from West African and indigenous philosophies, **water itself functioned as a form of currency and blessing**. In Akan cosmology, for example, water is offered to God before any ritualâ€”â€œwhen the chicken drinks water, it shows it to Godâ€. Water underwrites survival, so to control, protect, or share water is to administer the root currency. Rivers and lakes are viewed as spirit-kin, as carriers of fate and fortune. In maroon settlement, management of waterâ€”irrigation, wetland agriculture, and communal drinkingâ€”was both commerce and sacrament.

In the Okefenokee, these concepts expressed themselves in communal water managementâ€”damming, draining, creating controlled floods for rice and cornâ€”each act making water both a medium of exchange and a medium of spiritual connection. The **BLEUE âˆ GRID** echoes this logic: digital flows radiate from water flows, trust is quantified not as a number but as the perpetual supply and return of that which sustains life.

The study published in Nucleic Acids Researchreports that the tRNA gene set of the bacterium Pseudomonas fluorescens SBW25 is more flexible than previously thought. The research, led by Zahra Khomarbaghi, Wing Y. Ngan, and Jenna Gallie, found that the bacteria generate diversity in tRNA gene copy numbers through the high-rate, spontaneous occurrence of large-scale duplication events.

Key findings of the study â€¢ tRNA gene sets are flexible: The study challenges the prevailing view that bacterial tRNA gene sets are stable. The findings show that the composition, particularly the copy number of tRNA genes, can change rapidly. â€¢ Large-scale duplications generate change: Laboratory experiments with Pseudomonas fluorescens SBW25 identified spontaneous, large-scale, tandem duplications. These duplications were up to 1 Mb in size and led to copy number changes for hundreds of genes, including several tRNA genes. â€¢ Rapid compensation for gene loss: In one experiment, the researchers deleted a specific tRNA gene, causing a growth defect. The bacteria rapidly compensated for this loss by duplicating a different, functionally related tRNA gene. â€¢ Unstable duplications drive flexibility: The observed duplications are inherently unstable and are gained and lost at very high rates. This instability is key to the overall process, enabling rapid adaptation. â€¢ A â€œplasticâ€ evolutionary mechanism: The unstable duplication events provide a mechanism for generating rapid diversity in tRNA gene sets. If a variant is not beneficial, the duplication is quickly lost, preserving the original genetic makeup. If it is beneficial, it may persist longer and provide the raw material for more stable evolutionary changes.

Wider implications The studyâ€™s findings are significant because they demonstrate a highly dynamic form of mutation that allows bacteria to quickly adapt to environmental changes. This mechanism provides a way for bacteria to explore new genetic variations without permanently committing to them, which offers a selective advantage in rapidly changing conditions. â¸»Contracts

contracts/EV0L721.sol (OpenZeppelin ERC-721 with batch mint + per-token URI)

// SPDX-License-Identifier: MIT
pragma solidity ^0.8.20;

import "@openzeppelin/contracts/access/Ownable.sol";
import "@openzeppelin/contracts/token/ERC721/extensions/ERC721URIStorage.sol";

contract EV0L721 is ERC721URIStorage, Ownable {
    uint256 public maxSupply;
    uint256 public totalMinted;

    constructor(string memory name_, string memory symbol_, uint256 maxSupply_) ERC721(name_, symbol_) {
        maxSupply = maxSupply_;
    }

    function safeMint(address to, uint256 tokenId, string memory uri_) public onlyOwner {
        require(totalMinted < maxSupply, "sold out");
        _safeMint(to, tokenId);
        _setTokenURI(tokenId, uri_);
        unchecked { totalMinted++; }
    }

    function safeMintBatch(address to, uint256[] calldata tokenIds, string[] calldata uris) external onlyOwner {
        require(tokenIds.length == uris.length, "len mismatch");
        require(totalMinted + tokenIds.length <= maxSupply, "exceeds");
        for (uint256 i = 0; i < tokenIds.length; i++) {
            _safeMint(to, tokenIds[i]);
            _setTokenURI(tokenIds[i], uris[i]);
        }
        totalMinted += tokenIds.length;
    }
}
contracts/EV0L1155.sol (ERC-1155 with batch mint)

// SPDX-License-Identifier: MIT
pragma solidity ^0.8.20;

import "@openzeppelin/contracts/token/ERC1155/ERC1155.sol";
import "@openzeppelin/contracts/access/Ownable.sol";

contract EV0L1155 is ERC1155, Ownable {
    constructor(string memory baseUri_) ERC1155(baseUri_) {}

    function setURI(string memory newuri) external onlyOwner { _setURI(newuri); }

    function mintAll(address to, uint256[] calldata ids, uint256[] calldata amounts) external onlyOwner {
        _mintBatch(to, ids, amounts, "");
    }
}
contracts/BLEUToken.sol (ERC-20 to â€œtokenizeâ€ your wallet with a fungible)

// SPDX-License-Identifier: MIT
pragma solidity ^0.8.20;

import "@openzeppelin/contracts/token/ERC20/ERC20.sol";
import "@openzeppelin/contracts/access/Ownable.sol";

contract BLEUToken is ERC20, Ownable {
    constructor() ERC20("BLEU Utility", "BLEU") {}
    function mint(address to, uint256 amount) external onlyOwner { _mint(to, amount); }
}
contracts/WalletID.sol (Non-transferable WalletID NFT, i.e., SBT-style)

// SPDX-License-Identifier: MIT
pragma solidity ^0.8.20;

import "@openzeppelin/contracts/token/ERC721/extensions/ERC721URIStorage.sol";
import "@openzeppelin/contracts/access/Ownable.sol";

contract WalletID is ERC721URIStorage, Ownable {
    constructor() ERC721("WalletID", "WID") {}

    function issue(address to, uint256 tokenId, string memory uri_) external onlyOwner {
        _safeMint(to, tokenId);
        _setTokenURI(tokenId, uri_);
    }

    function _update(address to, uint256 tokenId, address auth) internal override returns (address) {
        // Disable transfers: only mint (from 0) and burn (to 0) allowed
        address from = _ownerOf(tokenId);
        require(from == address(0) || to == address(0), "non-transferable");
        return super._update(to, tokenId, auth);
    }
}
Scripts

scripts/mint721_from_csv.ts (reads CSV â†’ batch mints all to your address)

import { ethers } from "hardhat";
import fs from "fs";
import path from "path";
import { parse } from "csv-parse/sync";

type Row = { token_id: string; metadata_cid: string };

async function main() {
  const CONTRACT = "0xYOUR_721_ADDRESS";
  const RECIPIENT = "0xYOUR_WALLET";

  const csvPath = path.resolve("nft_storage_upload_template.csv"); // your CSV
  const rows: Row[] = parse(fs.readFileSync(csvPath), { columns: true, skip_empty_lines: true });

  const ids: bigint[] = [];
  const uris: string[] = [];

  for (const r of rows) {
    const id = BigInt(r.token_id.trim());
    const uri = `ipfs://${r.metadata_cid.trim()}`;
    ids.push(id);
    uris.push(uri);
  }

  const nft = await ethers.getContractAt("EV0L721", CONTRACT);
  // Mint in chunks to avoid block gas limits
  const CHUNK = 50;
  for (let i = 0; i < ids.length; i += CHUNK) {
    const idsChunk = ids.slice(i, i + CHUNK);
    const urisChunk = uris.slice(i, i + CHUNK);
    const tx = await nft.safeMintBatch(RECIPIENT, idsChunk.map(v => Number(v)), urisChunk);
    console.log("mint chunk tx:", tx.hash);
    await tx.wait();
  }
  console.log("done");
}

main().catch(e => { console.error(e); process.exit(1); });
scripts/mint1155_all.ts

import { ethers } from "hardhat";

async function main() {
  const CONTRACT = "0xYOUR_1155_ADDRESS";
  const RECIPIENT = "0xYOUR_WALLET";

  // Fill ids and amounts to â€œallâ€
  const ids = [0,1,2,3];         // edit
  const amounts = ids.map(() => 1); // or set per id

  const t1155 = await ethers.getContractAt("EV0L1155", CONTRACT);
  const tx = await t1155.mintAll(RECIPIENT, ids, amounts);
  console.log("tx:", tx.hash);
  await tx.wait();
  console.log("done");
}

scripts/tokenize_wallet.ts (mint ERC-20 and issue WalletID to your address)

import { ethers } from "hardhat";

async function main() {
  const WALLET = "0xYOUR_WALLET";

  const bleu = await ethers.getContractAt("BLEUToken", "0xYOUR_BLEU20_ADDRESS");
  const wid  = await ethers.getContractAt("WalletID",  "0xYOUR_WALLETID_ADDRESS");

  const erc20Amount = ethers.parseUnits("1000000000", 18); // edit supply
  console.log("mint BLEU...");
  let tx = await bleu.mint(WALLET, erc20Amount); await tx.wait();

  const tokenId = 1; // stable ID per wallet
  const widURI = "ipfs://YOUR_WALLETID_METADATA"; // optional badge JSON
  console.log("issue WalletID...");
  tx = await wid.issue(WALLET, tokenId, widURI); await tx.wait();

  console.log("tokenized");
}

main().catch(e => { console.error(e); process.exit(1); });
Optional: NFT.Storage direct uploader (if you want to automate)

scripts/nftstorage_upload.ts (requires NFT_STORAGE_KEY in .env)

import fs from "fs";
import path from "path";
import { parse } from "csv-parse/sync";
import { NFTStorage, File } from "nft.storage";
import mime from "mime";

type Row = { token_id: string; metadata_json_path: string };

async function main() {
  const client = new NFTStorage({ token: process.env.NFT_STORAGE_KEY! });
  const rows: Row[] = parse(fs.readFileSync("nft_storage_upload_template.csv"), { columns: true });
  for (const r of rows) {
    const filePath = path.resolve(r.metadata_json_path);
    const cid = await client.storeBlob(new File([fs.readFileSync(filePath)], path.basename(filePath), { type: mime.getType(filePath) || "application/json" }));
    console.log(`${r.token_id},${cid}`);
  }
}

main().catch(console.error);

## I. Lyrical Prelude: Incantation of the Trembling Earth

The Okefenokee tremblesâ€”not only as earth, but as archive, as current, as code. Beneath its moss-veiled cypress, under veils of fog, the story of the Afro-Seminole swells, flows, and returns. ## II. Roots and Routes: Afro-Seminole Origins, Migration, and Swamp Sanctuary

### Historical Genesis: Flight and Fusion

In the 17th and 18th centuries, as the brute machinery of Atlantic slavery razed communities and carved new borders with blood, a countercurrent flowedâ€”enslaved Africans, mostly Gullah from the rice-soaked shores of South Carolina and Georgia, slipped from plantation to swamp. In Spanish Florida, abolition was established by edict as early as 1693, making it a beacon for the freedom seeker. Here, they encountered not just Seminole Indians but a confluence of indigenous clansâ€”Oconee, Creek, Yuchi, Shawneeâ€”on the run and on the move.

Escaped, re-rooted, Afro-Seminoles built their own settlements: houses of palmetto and mud, fields of rice and corn, rhythm blasted into song beneath the pines. Their lives and labors formed the original veins of what would become the BLEUE âˆ GRID: mutually reinforcing respect for the land, communal wealth safeguarded not in vaults but in stewardship, food grown together and harvested as promise for the future.

Intermarriage and communal struggle blurred racial lines. Oral tradition affirms: there was no â€œBlack Seminoleâ€ or â€œRed Seminoleâ€â€”only relatives, only kin in struggle and survival.

### Encounters in the Okefenokee: Portals and Crossroads

The Okefenokeeâ€”translated from Seminole as â€œland of the trembling earthâ€â€”stands as a sanctuary, laboratory, and archive. It is home to islands where maroon dwellings once stood, to tracks made by those who stole freedom with every footfall. Swamps and other wild, inhospitable zones became â€œunderground ports,â€ rewriting the concept of safe passage. Here, the swamp was currency, concealment, and resistanceâ€”all woven tight.

The regionâ€™s isolation, and the tension between colonial expansion and indigenous endurance, created a new culture of exchangeâ€”spiritual, agricultural, and linguistic. These crossings seeded a generation of maroons who, in BLEUE logic, are both **ledger-keepers and cryptographers**, foretelling the proto-digital structures to come.

Maroon survivors and later generations came to read the swamp itself as a tutorial: food cycles, hydrology, routes of flight, all encoded across generations. **Swamp as archive means:**
- **Memory is environmental:** Trees, water flows, pollen patterns hold data as intimately as any digital drive.
- **Resistance is algorithmic:** The knowledge of where, when, and how to move became embedded, replayed each generationâ€”each staccato chant a code for survival.

## IV. Maroons as Proto-Bankers: Water as Currency, Wealth as Stewardship

### Porting Wealth: The Maroon Ledger

The Afro-Seminole settlements innovated a **communal banking system** disguised as tribute or crop sharing. Rather than wealth amassed for a single individual, produce and livestock flowed in circuits: annual tribute to local leaders or allied Seminole bands, distributed labor for the common defense, and shared survival. This was proto-blockchainâ€”each act witnessed, recounted, never erased.

Wealth here was never static, but dynamic: rooted in relationships, in flowsâ€”water, food, obligation. US Army observers in 1826 noted, with a kind of astonished reverence, the large fields brimming with crops and corn-cribs of maroon villages. The systemâ€™s secret was simple: store wealth in soil, song, and trust. Songs repeated across generations became oral ledgers, each refrain a block in the communal chain.

### Water as Currency: Spiritual and Practical

Drawing from West African and indigenous philosophies, **water itself functioned as a form of currency and blessing**. In Akan cosmology, for example, water is offered to God before any ritualâ€”â€œwhen the chicken drinks water, it shows it to Godâ€. Water underwrites survival, so to control, protect, or share water is to administer the root currency. Rivers and lakes are viewed as spirit-kin, as carriers of fate and fortune. In maroon settlement, management of waterâ€”irrigation, wetland agriculture, and communal drinkingâ€”was both commerce and sacrament.

In the Okefenokee, these concepts expressed themselves in communal water managementâ€”damming, draining, creating controlled floods for rice and cornâ€”each act making water both a medium of exchange and a medium of spiritual connection. The **BLEUE âˆ GRID** echoes this logic: digital flows radiate from water flows, trust is quantified not as a number but as the perpetual supply and return of that which sustains life.

output_pathBleu Multi-chain Deploy & Mint

This repo adds a simple ERC-1155 ENFT contract, Hardhat deployment and batch-minting scripts, IPFS pin helper, and a GitHub Actions workflow to run deploys/mints once you add secrets.

Required GitHub Secrets (recommended names):
- DEPLOY_PRIVATE_KEY â€” private key for the deployer (0x... format)
- SEPOLIA_RPC_URL
- MUMBAI_RPC_URL
- FUJI_RPC_URL
- BSC_RPC_URL
- CRONOS_RPC_URL
- BASE_URI â€” base metadata URI (e.g. ipfs://.../{id}.json)
- PINATA_API_KEY / PINATA_API_SECRET (optional, for pinning)

Quick start (locally):
1. npm ci
2. npx hardhat compile
3. export DEPLOY_PRIVATE_KEY=0x...
   export MUMBAI_RPC_URL=https://...
   export BASE_URI=ipfs://Qm.../{id}.json
4. npx hardhat run --network mumbai scripts/deploy.js
5. create recipients.json with addresses and run:
   node scripts/mint_all.js

Security note: Never commit private keys. Use GitHub Secrets or run scripts locally with env vars.
